<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artificial_photosynthesis">Artificial photosynthesis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Artificial photosynthesis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Artificial_photosynthesis" title="Artificial photosynthesis">Artificial photosynthesis</a></div>
<p>Artificial photosynthesis uses techniques including <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a> to store solar electromagnetic energy in chemical bonds by splitting water to produce hydrogen and then using carbon dioxide to make methanol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Researchers in this field strived to design molecular mimics of photosynthesis that use a wider region of the solar spectrum, employ catalytic systems made from abundant, inexpensive materials that are robust, readily repaired, non-toxic, stable in a variety of environmental conditions and perform more efficiently allowing a greater proportion of photon energy to end up in the storage compounds, i.e., carbohydrates (rather than building and sustaining living cells).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faunce_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-faunce-122">[122]</a></sup> However, prominent research faces hurdles, Sun Catalytix a MIT spin-off stopped scaling up their prototype fuel-cell in 2012, because it offers few savings over other ways to make hydrogen from sunlight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_infrared_thermal_radiation">Earth infrared thermal radiation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Earth infrared thermal radiation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Earth emits roughly 10<sup>17</sup> W of infrared thermal radiation that flows toward the cold outer space. Solar energy hits the surface and atmosphere of the earth and produces heat. Using various theorized devices like emissive energy harvester (EEH) or thermoradiative diode, this energy flow can be converted into electricity. In theory, this technology can be used during nighttime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Algae_fuels">Algae fuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Algae fuels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algae_fuels" title="Algae fuels">Algae fuels</a></div>
<p>Producing liquid fuels from oil-rich (fat-rich) varieties of algae is an ongoing research topic. Various microalgae grown in open or closed systems are being tried including some systems that can be set up in brownfield and desert lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_vapor">Water vapor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Water vapor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Collection of static electricity charges from water droplets on metal surfaces is an experimental technology that would be especially useful in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">low-income countries</a> with relative air humidity over 60%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crop_wastes">Crop wastes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Crop wastes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>AuREUS devices (Aurora Renewable Energy &amp; UV Sequestration),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> which are based on crop wastes can absorb <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> light from the sun and turn it into renewable energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Integration_into_the_energy_system_and_sector_coupling">Integration into the energy system and sector coupling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Integration into the energy system and sector coupling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">Variable renewable energy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3201" data-file-width="4168" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png/220px-Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png/330px-Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png/440px-Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Renewables_need_flexible_backup_not_baseload.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estimated power demand over a week in 2012 and 2020, Germany, showing the need for <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable generation</a> rather than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseload" title="Baseload">baseload</a> generation in the grid.</div></div></div>
<p>Renewable energy production from some sources such as wind and solar is more variable and more geographically spread than technology based on fossil fuels and nuclear. While integrating it into the wider energy system is feasible, it does lead to some additional challenges such as increased production volatility and decreased system inertia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olauson_16175_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olauson_16175-131">[131]</a></sup> Implementation of energy storage, using a wide variety of renewable energy technologies, and implementing a <a href="/wiki/Smart_grid" title="Smart grid">smart grid</a> in which energy is automatically used at the moment it is produced can reduce risks and costs of renewable energy implementation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olauson_16175_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-Olauson_16175-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIPCC201115–16_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC201115–16-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sector coupling of the power generation sector with other sectors may increase flexibility: for example the transport sector can be coupled by charging electric vehicles and sending electricity from <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">vehicle to grid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Similarly the industry sector can be coupled by hydrogen produced by electrolysis,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and the buildings sector by thermal energy storage for space heating and cooling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrical_energy_storage">Electrical energy storage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Electrical energy storage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Energy_storage" title="Energy storage">Energy storage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">Grid energy storage</a></div>
<p>Electrical energy storage is a collection of methods used to store electrical energy. Electrical energy is stored during times when production (especially from intermittent sources such as <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tidal_power" title="Tidal power">tidal power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>) exceeds consumption, and returned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_grid" title="Power grid">grid</a> when production falls below consumption. <a href="/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity" title="Pumped-storage hydroelectricity">Pumped-storage hydroelectricity</a> accounts for more than 85% of all <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid power storage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Batteries are increasingly being deployed for this<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and for grid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancillary_services" title="Ancillary services">ancillary services</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> and for domestic storage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Market_and_industry_trends">Market and industry trends<span class="anchor" id="Economic_trends"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Market and industry trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">Renewable energy commercialization</a></div>
<p>Most new renewables are solar, followed by wind then hydro then bioenergy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 5">: 5 </span></sup> Investment in renewables, especially solar, tends to be more effective in creating jobs than coal, gas or oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Worldwide, renewables employ about 12 million people as of 2020, with solar PV being the technology employing the most at almost 4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_of_renewables">Growth of renewables</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Growth of renewables">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:592px;max-width:592px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader">Pricing</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:155px;max-width:155px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:131px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="2478" data-file-width="2879" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png/153px-3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png/230px-3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png/306px-3-Learning-curves-for-electricity-prices.png 2x" width="153"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">A comparison of prices over time for energy from wind, solar and other sources. Over time, renewables benefit from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Learning_curves" title="Learning curves">learning curves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:254px;max-width:254px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:131px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_(LCOE,_Lazard)_-_renewable_energy.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1150" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg/252px-20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg/378px-20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg/504px-20201019_Levelized_Cost_of_Energy_%28LCOE%2C_Lazard%29_-_renewable_energy.svg.png 2x" width="252"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Levelized cost: With increasingly widespread implementation of renewable energy sources, costs have declined, most notably for energy generated by solar panels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LazardPopSci_costs_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-LazardPopSci_costs-148">[148]</a></sup>
<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levelized_cost_of_energy" title="Levelized cost of energy">Levelized cost of energy</a> (LCOE) is a measure of the average net present cost of electricity generation for a generating plant over its lifetime.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:177px;max-width:177px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:131px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg/175px-2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg/263px-2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg/350px-2010-_Cost_of_renewable_energy_-_IRENA.svg.png 2x" width="175"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Past costs of producing renewable energy declined significantly, with 62% of total renewable power generation added in 2020 having lower costs than the cheapest new fossil fuel option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA_20210622_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA_20210622-149">[149]</a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The results of a recent review of the literature concluded that as <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> (GHG) emitters begin to be held liable for damages resulting from GHG emissions resulting in climate change, a high value for liability mitigation would provide powerful incentives for deployment of renewable energy technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the decade of 2010–2019, worldwide investment in renewable energy capacity excluding large hydropower amounted to US$2.7 trillion, of which the top countries China contributed US$818 billion, the United States contributed US$392.3 billion, Japan contributed US$210.9 billion, Germany contributed US$183.4 billion, and the United Kingdom contributed US$126.5 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020gt-c4d_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-2020gt-c4d-151">[151]</a></sup> This was an increase of over three and possibly four times the equivalent amount invested in the decade of 2000–2009 (no data is available for 2000–2003).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020gt-c4d_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-2020gt-c4d-151">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_projections">Future projections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Future projections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition" title="Energy transition">Energy transition</a></div>
<p>A May 2022 report by the IEA predicted renewables to remain competitive in 2023 despite rising costs, as fossil fuel costs have risen much faster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-140">[140]</a></sup> The report forecasts almost 200 GW of solar PV to be installed in 2023.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_140-2"><a href="#cite_note-:5-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 8">: 8 </span></sup> China and Europe are both expected to install  more renewables than the US, due to uncertainty in <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_the_United_States" title="Energy policy of the United States">US energy policy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_140-3"><a href="#cite_note-:5-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 13">: 13 </span></sup> The report forecasts biofuel demand to increase in India and Indonesia in 2023, partly due to their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transport_policy" title="Transport policy">transport policies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_140-4"><a href="#cite_note-:5-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 22">: 22 </span></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022 IEA Executive Director <a href="/wiki/Fatih_Birol" title="Fatih Birol">Fatih Birol</a> said that countries should invest more in renewables to "ease the pressure on consumers from high fossil fuel prices, make our energy systems more secure, and get the world on track to reach our climate goals.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>China's <a href="/wiki/Five-year_plans_of_China#Fourteenth_Plan_(2021–2025)" title="Five-year plans of China">five year plan to 2025</a> includes increasing direct heating by renewables such as geothermal and solar thermal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/REPowerEU" title="REPowerEU">REPowerEU</a>, the EU plan to escape <a href="/wiki/Russia_in_the_European_energy_sector" title="Russia in the European energy sector">dependence on fossil Russian gas</a>, is expected to call for much more <a href="/wiki/Green_hydrogen" title="Green hydrogen">green hydrogen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demand">Demand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2014, <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Resources_Institute" title="World Resources Institute">World Resources Institute</a> convened a discussion among a number of major US companies who had declared their intention to increase their use of renewable energy. These discussions identified a number of "principles" which companies seeking greater access to renewable energy considered important market deliverables. These principles included choice (between suppliers and between products), cost competitiveness, longer term fixed price supplies, access to third-party financing vehicles, and collaboration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>UK statistics released in September 2020 noted that "the proportion of demand met from renewables varies from a low of 3.4 per cent (for transport, mainly from biofuels) to highs of over 20 per cent for 'other final users', which is largely the service and commercial sectors that consume relatively large quantities of electricity, and industry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>In some locations, individual households can opt to purchase renewable energy through a <a href="/wiki/Consumer_green_energy_program" title="Consumer green energy program">consumer green energy program</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trends_for_individual_technologies">Trends for individual technologies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Trends for individual technologies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydroelectricity">Hydroelectricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Hydroelectricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2020 the world renewable hydropower capacity was 1,330 GW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iha2021_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-iha2021-157">[157]</a></sup> Only a third of the world's estimated hydroelectric potential of 14,000 TWh/year has been developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iha2021_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-iha2021-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etp2006_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-etp2006-158">[158]</a></sup> New hydropower projects face opposition from local communities due to their large impact, including relocation of communities and flooding of wildlife habitats and farming land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> High cost and lead times from permission process, including environmental and risk assessments, with lack of environmental and social acceptance are therefore the primary challenges for new developments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> It is popular to repower old dams thereby increasing their efficiency and capacity as well as quicker responsiveness on the grid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Where circumstances permit existing dams such as the <a href="/wiki/Richard_B._Russell_Dam" title="Richard B. Russell Dam">Russell Dam</a> built in 1985 may be updated with "pump back" facilities for <a href="/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity" title="Pumped-storage hydroelectricity">pumped-storage</a> which is useful for peak loads or to support intermittent wind and solar power. Because <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable power</a> is more valuable than VRE<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> countries with large hydroelectric developments such as Canada and Norway are spending billions to expand their grids to trade with neighboring countries having limited hydro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_power_development">Wind power development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Wind power development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_by_country"
