The latter is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_offshore_wind_farms" title="List of offshore wind farms">largest in the world</a> as of April 2013.</div></div></div>
<dl><dd>Offshore wind is becoming more profitable <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_thermal">Solar thermal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Solar thermal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_solar_thermal_power_stations" title="List of solar thermal power stations">List of solar thermal power stations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IvanpahRunning.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/IvanpahRunning.JPG/220px-IvanpahRunning.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/IvanpahRunning.JPG/330px-IvanpahRunning.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/IvanpahRunning.JPG/440px-IvanpahRunning.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IvanpahRunning.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 377 MW <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivanpah_Solar_Electric_Generating_System" title="Ivanpah Solar Electric Generating System">Ivanpah Solar Electric Generating System</a> with all three towers under load, February 2014. Taken from I-15.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PS20andPS10.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1025" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/PS20andPS10.jpg/220px-PS20andPS10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/PS20andPS10.jpg/330px-PS20andPS10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/PS20andPS10.jpg/440px-PS20andPS10.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PS20andPS10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solar towers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PS10" title="PS10">PS10</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PS20" title="PS20">PS20</a> <a href="/wiki/Concentrated_solar_power" title="Concentrated solar power">solar thermal plants</a> in Spain</div></div></div>
<p>Solar thermal energy capacity has increased from 1.3 GW in 2012 to 5.0 GW in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_power_in_Spain" title="Solar thermal power in Spain">Spain</a> is the world leader in solar thermal power deployment with 2.3 GW deployed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_States#Concentrated_solar_power_(CSP)" title="Solar power in the United States">United States</a> has 1.8 GW,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-2"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup> most of it in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_power_in_California" title="Solar thermal power in California">California</a> where 1.4 GW of solar thermal power projects are operational.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Several power plants have been constructed in the <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_plants_in_the_Mojave_Desert" title="Solar power plants in the Mojave Desert">Mojave Desert</a>, Southwestern United States. As of 2017 only 4 other countries have deployments above 100 MW:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-3"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_South_Africa#Solar_Thermal_Energy" title="Solar power in South Africa">South Africa</a> (300 MW) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_power_in_India" title="Solar thermal power in India">India</a> (229 MW) <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Morocco" title="Solar power in Morocco">Morocco</a> (180 MW) and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Solar power in the United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (100 MW).
</p><p>The United States conducted much early research in photovoltaics and <a href="/wiki/Concentrated_solar_power" title="Concentrated solar power">concentrated solar power</a>. The U.S. is among the top countries in the world in electricity generated by the Sun and several of the world's largest utility-scale installations are located in the desert Southwest.
</p><p>The oldest <a href="/wiki/List_of_solar_thermal_power_stations" title="List of solar thermal power stations">solar thermal power plant</a> in the world is the 354 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megawatt" title="Megawatt">megawatt</a> (MW) <a href="/wiki/Solar_Energy_Generating_Systems" title="Solar Energy Generating Systems">SEGS thermal power plant</a>, in California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivanpah_Solar_Electric_Generating_System" title="Ivanpah Solar Electric Generating System">Ivanpah Solar Electric Generating System</a> is a solar thermal power project in the California <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave Desert</a>, 40 miles (64 km) southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a>, with a gross capacity of 377 MW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-woody_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-woody-169">[169]</a></sup> The 280 MW <a href="/wiki/Solana_Generating_Station" title="Solana Generating Station">Solana Generating Station</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> plant near <a href="/wiki/Gila_Bend,_Arizona" title="Gila Bend, Arizona">Gila Bend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, about 70 miles (110 km) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a>, completed in 2013. When commissioned it was the largest parabolic trough plant in the world and the first U.S. solar plant with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molten_salt_thermal_storage" title="Molten salt thermal storage">molten salt thermal energy storage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>In developing countries, three <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> projects for integrated solar thermal/combined-cycle gas-turbine power plants in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> have been approved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Status_Report200812_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Status_Report200812-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Photovoltaic_development">Photovoltaic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Photovoltaic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox current red Americas.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2019</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_photovoltaics" title="Growth of photovoltaics">Growth of photovoltaics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_by_country" title="Solar power by country">Solar power by country</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_photovoltaic_power_stations" title="List of photovoltaic power stations">List of photovoltaic power stations</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Photovoltaics" title="Photovoltaics">Photovoltaics</a> (PV) is rapidly-growing with global capacity increasing from 177 GW at the end of 2014 to 385 GW in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-4"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>PV uses <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell" title="Solar cell">solar cells</a> assembled into <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">solar panels</a> to convert sunlight into electricity. <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_system" title="Photovoltaic system">PV systems</a> range from small, residential and commercial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rooftop_photovoltaic_power_station" title="Rooftop photovoltaic power station">rooftop</a> or <a href="/wiki/Building-integrated_photovoltaics" title="Building-integrated photovoltaics">building integrated</a> installations, to large utility-scale <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_power_station" title="Photovoltaic power station">photovoltaic power station</a>. The predominant PV technology is <a href="/wiki/Crystalline_silicon" title="Crystalline silicon">crystalline silicon</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Thin-film_solar_cell" title="Thin-film solar cell">thin-film solar cell</a> technology accounts for about 10 percent of global photovoltaic deployment. In recent years, PV technology has improved its electricity generating <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell_efficiency" title="Solar cell efficiency">efficiency</a>, reduced the installation <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Price_per_watt" title="Price per watt">cost per watt</a> as well as its <a href="/wiki/Crystalline_silicon#Energy_payback_time" title="Crystalline silicon">energy payback time</a>, and reached <a href="/wiki/Grid_parity" title="Grid parity">grid parity</a> in at least 30 different markets by 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deutsche-2015-chasm_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-deutsche-2015-chasm-172">[172]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Building-integrated_photovoltaics" title="Building-integrated photovoltaics">Building-integrated photovoltaics</a> or "onsite" PV systems use existing land and structures and generate power close to where it is consumed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>Photovoltaics grew fastest in <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_China" title="Solar power in China">China</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Japan" title="Solar power in Japan">Japan</a> and the United States. Solar power is forecasted to become the world's largest source of electricity by 2050, with solar photovoltaics and concentrated solar power contributing 16% and 11%, respectively. This requires an increase of installed PV capacity to 4,600 GW, of which more than half is expected to be deployed in China and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_India" title="Solar power in India">India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IEA-roadmap-PV-2014_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-IEA-roadmap-PV-2014-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_(8159002527)_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_%288159002527%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_%288159002527%29_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_%288159002527%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_%288159002527%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_%288159002527%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_%288159002527%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solar_Panels_at_Topaz_Solar_1_(8159002527)_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">Solar panels</a> at the 550 MW <a href="/wiki/Topaz_Solar_Farm" title="Topaz Solar Farm">Topaz Solar Farm</a></div></div></div>
<p>Commercial concentrated solar power plants were first developed in the 1980s. As the cost of solar electricity has fallen, the number of grid-connected solar PV systems has <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_photovoltaics" title="Growth of photovoltaics">grown into the millions</a> and utility-scale <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_power_station" title="Photovoltaic power station">solar power stations</a> with hundreds of megawatts are being built. Many solar photovoltaic power stations have been built, mainly in Europe, China and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PV_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-PV-175">[175]</a></sup> The 1.5 GW <a href="/wiki/Tengger_Desert_Solar_Park" title="Tengger Desert Solar Park">Tengger Desert Solar Park</a>, in China is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_photovoltaic_power_stations" title="List of photovoltaic power stations">world's largest PV power station</a>. Many of these plants are integrated with agriculture and some use tracking systems that follow the sun's daily path across the sky to generate more electricity than fixed-mounted systems.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Biofuel_development">Biofuel development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Biofuel development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">Ethanol fuel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_biofuel" title="Sustainable biofuel">Sustainable biofuel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Issues_relating_to_biofuels" title="Issues relating to biofuels">Issues relating to biofuels</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg/220px-Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg/330px-Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg/440px-Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_ethanol_pump_04_2008_74_zoom.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_Brazil" title="Ethanol fuel in Brazil">Brazil</a> produces <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">bioethanol</a> made from sugarcane available throughout the country. A typical gas station with dual fuel service is marked "A" for <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">alcohol (ethanol)</a> and "G" for gasoline.</div></div></div>
<p>Bioenergy global capacity in 2017 was 109 GW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-5"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup>
Biofuels provided 3% of the world's transport <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a> in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mandates for blending biofuels exist in 31 countries at the national level and in 29 states/provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Status_Report201113–14_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Status_Report201113–14-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_Brazil" title="Ethanol fuel in Brazil">Brazil has had an ethanol fuel program</a> which has allowed the country to become the world's second largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a> (after the United States) and the world's largest exporter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA1E_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-RFA1E-177">[177]</a></sup> Brazil's ethanol fuel program uses modern equipment and cheap <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> as feedstock, and the residual cane-waste (<a href="/wiki/Bagasse" title="Bagasse">bagasse</a>) is used to produce heat and power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_2004_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-MLA_2004-178">[178]</a></sup> There are no longer light vehicles in Brazil running on pure gasoline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-179">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biojet" title="Biojet">Biojet</a> is expected to be important for short-term reduction of carbon dioxide emissions from long-haul flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Geothermal_development">Geothermal development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Geothermal development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy_in_the_United_States" title="Geothermal energy in the United States">Geothermal energy in the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="2136" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG/170px-West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG/255px-West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG/340px-West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:West_Ford_Flat_Geothermal_Cooling_Tower.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geothermal plant at <a href="/wiki/The_Geysers" title="The Geysers">The Geysers</a>, California, US</div></div></div>
<p>Global geothermal capacity in 2017 was 12.9 GW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-6"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Geothermal power is cost effective, reliable, sustainable, and environmentally friendly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> but has historically been limited to areas near <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">tectonic plate</a> boundaries. Recent technological advances have expanded the range and size of viable resources, especially for applications such as home heating, opening a potential for widespread exploitation. Geothermal wells release greenhouse gases trapped deep within the earth, but these emissions are usually much lower per energy unit than those of fossil fuels. As a result, geothermal power has the potential to help mitigate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> if widely deployed in place of fossil fuels.
</p><p>In 2017, the United States led the world in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geothermal_electricity" title="Geothermal electricity">geothermal electricity</a> production with 12.9 GW of installed capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-7"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup> The largest group of geothermal power plants in the world is located at <a href="/wiki/The_Geysers" title="The Geysers">The Geysers</a>, a geothermal field in California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khan_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Khan-182">[182]</a></sup> The Philippines follows the US as the second highest producer of geothermal power in the world, with 1.9 GW of capacity online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA2018_166-8"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA2018-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Developing_countries">Developing countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Developing countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_developing_countries" title="Renewable energy in developing countries">Renewable energy in developing countries</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy_in_developing_countries&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang,_China.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang%2C_China.jpg/220px-Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang%2C_China.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang%2C_China.jpg/330px-Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang%2C_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang%2C_China.jpg/440px-Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang%2C_China.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_power_plants_in_Xinjiang,_China.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">Wind farm</a> in <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, China</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="285" data-file-width="322" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg/220px-Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/25/Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solar-Panel-Cooker-in-front-of-hut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Solar_cooker" title="Solar cooker">Solar cookers</a> use sunlight as energy source for outdoor cooking.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_developing_countries" title="Renewable energy in developing countries">Renewable energy in developing countries</a> is an increasingly used alternative to <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> energy, as these countries scale up their energy supplies and address <a href="/wiki/Energy_poverty" title="Energy poverty">energy poverty</a>. Renewable energy technology was once seen as unaffordable for developing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> However, since 2015, investment in non-hydro renewable energy has been higher in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a> than in developed countries, and comprised 54% of global renewable energy investment in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> forecasts that renewable energy will provide the majority of energy supply growth through 2030 in Africa and Central and South America, and 42% of supply growth in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
Most developing countries have abundant renewable energy resources, including <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal energy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a>, as well as the ability to manufacture the relatively labor-intensive systems that harness these. By developing such energy sources developing countries can reduce their dependence on oil and natural gas, creating energy portfolios that are less vulnerable to price rises. In many circumstances, these investments can be less expensive than fossil fuel energy systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Renewable_energy_in_developing_countries_mdg_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Renewable_energy_in_developing_countries_mdg-186">[186]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy">Policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Policies to support renewable energy have been vital in their expansion. Where Europe dominated in establishing energy policy in early 2000s, most countries around the world now have some form of energy policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-187">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_trends">Policy trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Policy trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Renewable_Energy_Agency" title="International Renewable Energy Agency">International Renewable Energy Agency</a> (IRENA) is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organization</a> for promoting the adoption of renewable energy worldwide. It aims to provide concrete policy advice and facilitate <a href="/wiki/Capacity_building" title="Capacity building">capacity building</a> and technology transfer. IRENA was formed in 2009, by 75 countries signing the charter of IRENA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> As of April 2019, IRENA has 160 member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The then United Nations' Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> has said that renewable energy has the ability to lift the poorest nations to new levels of prosperity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renewableenergyworld1_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-renewableenergyworld1-40">[40]</a></sup> and in September 2011 he launched the UN <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Energy_for_All" title="Sustainable Energy for All">Sustainable Energy for All</a> initiative to improve energy access, efficiency and the deployment of renewable energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2015 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> on climate change motivated many countries to develop or improve renewable energy policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Futures_Report2017_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Futures_Report2017-13">[13]</a></sup> In 2017, a total of 121 countries have adapted some form of renewable energy policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-187">[187]</a></sup> National targets that year existed in at 176 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Futures_Report2017_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Futures_Report2017-13">[13]</a></sup> In addition, there is also a wide range of policies at state/provincial and local levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Status_Report201113–14_103-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREN21_Renewables_Global_Status_Report201113–14-103">[103]</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Public_utility" title="Public utility">public utilities</a> help plan or install <a href="/wiki/Home_energy_upgrades_from_public_utilities" title="Home energy upgrades from public utilities">residential energy upgrades</a>.
</p><p>Many national, state, and local governments have created <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_bank_(financial_institution)" title="Green bank (financial institution)">green banks</a>. A green bank is a quasi-public financial institution that uses public capital to leverage private investment in clean energy technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Green banks use a variety of financial tools to bridge market gaps that hinder the deployment of clean energy.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_neutrality" title="Climate neutrality">Climate neutrality</a> by the year of 2050 is the main goal of the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Deal" title="European Green Deal">European Green Deal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> For the European union to reach their target of climate neutrality, one goal is to decarbonise their energy system by aiming to achieve "net-zero <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> by 2050."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Full_renewable_energy">Full renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Full renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">These paragraphs are an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% renewable energy</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=100%25_renewable_energy&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% renewable energy</a> means getting all energy from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_resource" title="Renewable resource">renewable resources</a>. The endeavor to use 100% renewable energy for electricity, heating, cooling and transport is motivated by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, pollution and other environmental issues, as well as economic and <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy security</a> concerns. Shifting the total global <a href="/wiki/Primary_energy" title="Primary energy">primary energy</a> supply to renewable sources requires <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_transition" title="Renewable energy transition">a transition of the energy system</a>, since most of today's energy is derived from non-renewable <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.
</p><p>Research into this topic is fairly new, with very few studies published before 2009, but has gained increasing attention in recent years. The majority of studies show that a global transition to 100% renewable energy across all sectors – power, heat, transport and desalination – is feasible and economically viable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_:3_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_:3-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_:8_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_:8-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_:6_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_:6-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_:7_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_:7-197">[197]</a></sup> A cross-sectoral, holistic approach is seen as an important feature of 100% renewable energy systems and is based on the assumption "that the best solutions can be found only if one focuses on the synergies between the sectors" of the energy system such as electricity, heat, transport or industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_Hansen_et_al._198-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_Hansen_et_al.-198">[198]</a></sup>
</p>
The main barriers to the widespread implementation of large-scale renewable energy and low-carbon energy strategies are seen to be primarily social and political rather than technological or economic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_Koumoundouros_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_Koumoundouros-199">[199]</a></sup> According to the 2013 <i>Post Carbon Pathways</i> report, which reviewed many international studies, the key roadblocks are: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">climate change denial</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels_lobby" title="Fossil fuels lobby">fossil fuels lobby</a>, political inaction, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">unsustainable energy consumption</a>, outdated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_infrastructure" title="Energy infrastructure">energy infrastructure</a>, and financial constraints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100%_renewable_energy_John_Wiseman_et_al_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-100%_renewable_energy_John_Wiseman_et_al-200">[200]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Debate">Debate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Debate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_debate" title="Renewable energy debate">Renewable energy debate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy" title="Nuclear power proposed as renewable energy">Nuclear power proposed as renewable energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_job" title="Green job">Green job</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intermittent_power_source" title="Intermittent power source">Intermittent power source</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation#Overviews,_strategies_and_comparisons_of_measures" title="Climate change mitigation">Climate change mitigation § Overviews, strategies and comparisons of measures</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="1700" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg/220px-Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg/330px-Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg/440px-Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Most_people_say_countries_should_back_renewable_energy_to_fight_climate_change.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Most respondents to a climate survey conducted in 2021-2022 by the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> say countries should back renewable energy to fight climate change. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Renewable electricity generation by wind and solar is <a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">variable</a>. This results in reduced <a href="/wiki/Capacity_factor" title="Capacity factor">capacity factor</a> and may require keeping some <a href="/wiki/Gas-fired_power_plant" title="Gas-fired power plant">gas-fired power plants</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable generation</a> on standby<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> until there is enough energy storage, <a href="/wiki/Demand_response" title="Demand response">demand response</a>, grid improvement, and/or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Base-load_power_plant" title="Base-load power plant">base load power</a> from non-intermittent sources like <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> or bioenergy.
</p><p>Solar power plants may compete with arable land,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_Zalk_Behrens_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-van_Zalk_Behrens-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> while on-shore wind farms face opposition due to aesthetic concerns and noise, which is impacting both humans and wildlife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In the United States, the Massachusetts <a href="/wiki/Cape_Wind" title="Cape Wind">Cape Wind</a> project was delayed for years partly because of aesthetic concerns. However, residents in other areas have been more positive. According to a town councilor, the overwhelming majority of locals believe that the <a href="/wiki/Ardrossan_Wind_Farm" title="Ardrossan Wind Farm">Ardrossan Wind Farm</a> in Scotland has enhanced the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-210">[210]</a></sup> These concerns, when directed against renewable energy, are sometimes described as "not in my back yard" attitude (<a href="/wiki/NIMBY" title="NIMBY">NIMBY</a>).
</p><p>A 2011 UK Government document states that "projects are generally more likely to succeed if they have broad public support and the consent of local communities. This means giving communities both a say and a stake".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> In countries such as Germany and Denmark many renewable projects are owned by communities, particularly through <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">cooperative</a> structures, and contribute significantly to overall levels of renewable energy deployment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>The market for renewable energy technologies has continued to grow. <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> concerns and increasing in <a href="/wiki/Green_job" title="Green job">green jobs</a>, coupled with high oil prices, <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">peak oil</a>, oil wars, <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil spills</a>, promotion of <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> and renewable electricity, nuclear disasters and increasing government support, are driving increasing renewable energy legislation, incentives and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">commercialization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEP_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="old (February 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> New government spending, regulation and policies helped the industry weather the 2009 economic crisis better than many other sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-obama-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> has stated that deployment of renewable technologies usually increases the diversity of electricity sources and, through local generation, contributes to the flexibility of the system and its resistance to central shocks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2021, European Commissioner for Climate Action <a href="/wiki/Frans_Timmermans" title="Frans Timmermans">Frans Timmermans</a> suggested "the best answer" to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2021_global_energy_crisis" title="2021 global energy crisis">2021 global energy crisis</a> is "to reduce our reliance on fossil fuels."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timmermans_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-Timmermans-215">[215]</a></sup> He said those blaming the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Deal" title="European Green Deal">European Green Deal</a> were doing so "for perhaps ideological reasons or sometimes economic reasons in protecting their vested interests."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timmermans_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-Timmermans-215">[215]</a></sup> Some critics blamed the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Emissions_Trading_System" title="European Union Emissions Trading System">European Union Emissions Trading System</a> (EU ETS) and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_phase-out" title="Nuclear power phase-out">closure of nuclear plants</a> for contributing to the energy crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> European Commission President <a href="/wiki/Ursula_von_der_Leyen" title="Ursula von der Leyen">Ursula von der Leyen</a> said that Europe is "too reliant" on natural gas and too <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_imports" title="List of countries by natural gas imports">dependent on natural gas imports</a>. According to Von der Leyen, "The answer has to do with diversifying our suppliers ... and, crucially, with speeding up the transition to clean energy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy">Nuclear power proposed as renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Nuclear power proposed as renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg/220px-2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg/330px-2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg/440px-2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011-05-10_18-57-46_Switzerland_-_Wil_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Leibstadt_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Leibstadt Nuclear Power Plant">Leibstadt Nuclear Power Plant</a> in Switzerland</div></div></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy" title="Nuclear power proposed as renewable energy">Nuclear power proposed as renewable energy</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>Whether <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> should be considered a form of renewable energy is an ongoing subject of debate. <a href="/wiki/Statute" title="Statute">Statutory</a> definitions of renewable energy usually exclude many present nuclear energy technologies, with the notable exception of the state of <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_Utah_House_Bill_430,_Session_198_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_Utah_House_Bill_430,_Session_198-220">[220]</a></sup> Dictionary-sourced definitions of renewable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_technologies" title="Energy technologies">energy technologies</a> often omit or explicitly exclude mention of nuclear energy sources, with an exception made for the natural nuclear <a href="/wiki/Decay_heat" title="Decay heat">decay heat</a> generated <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">within the Earth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_renewalt_basics_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_renewalt_basics-222">[222]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most common fuel used in conventional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_station" title="Nuclear power station">nuclear fission power stations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium-235" title="Uranium-235">uranium-235</a> is "non-renewable" according to the <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a>, the organization however is silent on the recycled <a href="/wiki/MOX_fuel" title="MOX fuel">MOX fuel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_renewalt_basics_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_renewalt_basics-222">[222]</a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Laboratory" title="National Renewable Energy Laboratory">National Renewable Energy Laboratory</a> does not mention nuclear power in its "energy basics" definition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
In 1987, the <a href="/wiki/Brundtland_Commission" title="Brundtland Commission">Brundtland Commission</a> (WCED) classified fission reactors that produce more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fissile" title="Fissile">fissile</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fuel" title="Nuclear fuel">nuclear fuel</a> than they consume (<a href="/wiki/Breeder_reactor" title="Breeder reactor">breeder reactors</a>, and if developed, <a href="/wiki/Fusion_power" title="Fusion power">fusion power</a>) among conventional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_sources" title="Renewable energy sources">renewable energy sources</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_Brundtland_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nuclear_power_proposed_as_renewable_energy_Brundtland-224">[224]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Petroleum_Institute" title="American Petroleum Institute">American Petroleum Institute</a> does not consider conventional nuclear fission renewable, but considers <a href="/wiki/Breeder_reactor" title="Breeder reactor">breeder reactor</a> nuclear fuel renewable and sustainable, and while conventional fission leads to waste streams that remain a concern for millennia, the waste from efficiently recycled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spent_fuel" title="Spent fuel">spent fuel</a> requires a more limited storage supervision period of about thousand years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> The monitoring and storage of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radioactive" title="Radioactive">radioactive</a> waste products is also required upon the use of other renewable energy sources, such as geothermal energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geopolitics_of_renewable_energy">Geopolitics of renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Geopolitics of renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Russia_in_the_European_energy_sector" title="Russia in the European energy sector">Russia in the European energy sector</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TREC-Map-en.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TREC-Map-en.jpg/220px-TREC-Map-en.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TREC-Map-en.jpg/330px-TREC-Map-en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TREC-Map-en.jpg/440px-TREC-Map-en.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TREC-Map-en.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A concept of a <a href="/wiki/Super_grid" title="Super grid">super grid</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>From around 2010 onwards, the geopolitical impact of the growing use of renewable energy has been discussed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Some argue that former fossil fuels exporters will experience a weakening of their position in international affairs, while countries with abundant renewable energy resources will be strengthened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Also some countries rich in critical materials for renewable energy technologies are expected to rise in importance in international affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup>
</p><p>The GeGaLo index of geopolitical gains and losses assesses how the geopolitical position of 156 countries may change if the world fully transitions to renewable energy resources. Former fossil fuels exporters are expected to lose power, while the positions of former fossil fuel importers and countries rich in renewable energy resources is expected to strengthen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several requirements and decisions that may be tied with geopolitical considerations are the sourcing of required materials, ownership of key infrastructure assets and the design of grids, including <a href="/wiki/Super_grid" title="Super grid">super grids</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (April 2022)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Transitions to renewable energy have many geopolitical implications such as the potential of revenue losses leading to political instability in insufficiently prepared fossil-fuel-exporting economies, albeit it is unclear whether the transition will increase or reduce conflict overall. In particular, a study hypothesizes that a "configuration emerges in which fossil fuel importers are better off decarbonizing, competitive fossil fuel exporters are better off flooding markets and uncompetitive fossil fuel producers—rather than benefitting from 'free-riding'—suffer from their exposure to stranded assets and lack of investment in decarbonization technologies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>A study found that transition from fossil fuels to renewable energy systems reduces risks from mining, trade and political dependence because renewable energy systems don't need fuel – they depend on trade only for the acquisition of materials and components during construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nations rich in solar and wind energy could become major energy exporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cb1_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-cb1-243">[243]</a></sup>
</p><p>Trade in hydrogen could fundamentally redraw the geography of the global energy trade, and international governance and investments that seek to scale up the <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_economy" title="Hydrogen economy">hydrogen economy</a> could reduce "the risk of market fragmentation, carbon lock-in, and intensified geo-economic rivalry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cb1_243-1"><a href="#cite_note-cb1-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wilsoncenter_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-wilsoncenter-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_environmental_impact">Health and environmental impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Health and environmental impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rare-earth_element#Environmental_considerations" title="Rare-earth element">Rare-earth element § Environmental considerations</a></div>
<p>Moving to modern renewable energy has very large health benefits due to reducing <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> from fossil fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup>
</p><p>Renewable sources other than biomass such as <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaics" title="Photovoltaics">photovoltaics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> have the advantage of being able to conserve water, lower pollution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> and reduce CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub> emissions.
</p><p>Solar panels change the <a href="/wiki/Albedo" title="Albedo">albedo</a> of the surface, so if used on a very large scale (such as covering 20% of the Sahara Desert), could change global weather patterns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomass">Biomass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Biomass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Biomass#Environmental_damage" title="Biomass">Biomass § Environmental damage</a></div>
<p>The ability of <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biofuels" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a> to contribute to a reduction in CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub> emissions is limited because both biomass and biofuels emit large amounts of air pollution when burned and in some cases compete with food supply. Furthermore, biomass and biofuels consume large amounts of water<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> and land (sometimes land that could be used for food production).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1016/j.rser.2016.12.109_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-10.1016/j.rser.2016.12.109-252">[252]</a></sup> Furthermore, there can be carbon leakage from biomass production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1016/j.rser.2016.12.109_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-10.1016/j.rser.2016.12.109-252">[252]</a></sup> Nevertheless, it could still help reduce carbon dioxide emissions<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> and play an important role as a method of <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable generation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Conservation_areas.2C_recycling_and_rare-earth_elements"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_areas,_recycling_and_rare-earth_elements">Conservation areas, recycling and rare-earth elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Conservation areas, recycling and rare-earth elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_aspects_of_the_electric_car" title="Environmental aspects of the electric car">Environmental aspects of the electric car</a></div>
<p>Installations used to produce wind, solar and hydropower are an increasing threat to key conservation areas, with facilities built in areas set aside for nature conservation and other environmentally sensitive areas. They are often much larger than fossil fuel power plants, needing areas of land up to 10 times greater than coal or gas to produce equivalent energy amounts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> More than 2000 renewable energy facilities are built, and more are under construction, in areas of environmental importance and threaten the habitats of plant and animal species across the globe. The authors' team emphasized that their work should not be interpreted as anti-renewables because renewable energy is crucial for reducing carbon emissions. The key is ensuring that renewable energy facilities are built in places where they do not damage biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition" title="Energy transition">transition to renewable energy</a> depends on non-renewable resources, such as mined metals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_Zalk_Behrens_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-van_Zalk_Behrens-205">[205]</a></sup> Manufacturing of photovoltaic panels, wind turbines and batteries requires significant amounts of <a href="/wiki/Rare-earth_element" title="Rare-earth element">rare-earth elements</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-261">[261]</a></sup> which has significant social and environmental impact if mined in forests and protected areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup>  Due to co-occurrence of rare-earth and radioactive elements (<a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radium" title="Radium">radium</a>), rare-earth mining results in production of low-level <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_waste" title="Radioactive waste">radioactive waste</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020 scientists published a <a href="/wiki/World_map" title="World map">world map</a> of areas that contain renewable energy materials as well as estimations of their overlaps with "Key Biodiversity Areas", "Remaining Wilderness" and "<a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">Protected Areas</a>". The authors assessed that careful <a href="/wiki/Strategic_planning" title="Strategic planning">strategic planning</a> is needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell#Recycling" title="Solar cell">Solar panels are recycled</a> to reduce <a href="/wiki/Electronic_waste" title="Electronic waste">electronic waste</a> and create a source for materials that would otherwise need to be mined,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> but such business is still small and work is ongoing to improve and scale-up the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-techrev_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-techrev-268">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Prior to the development of coal in the mid 19th century, nearly all energy used was renewable. The oldest known use of renewable energy, in the form of traditional <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a> to <a href="/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans" title="Control of fire by early humans">fuel fires</a>, dates from more than a million years ago. The use of biomass for fire did not become commonplace until many hundreds of thousands of years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fire_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fire-271">[271]</a></sup> Probably the second oldest usage of renewable energy is harnessing the wind in order to drive ships over water. This practice can be traced back some 7000 years, to ships in the Persian Gulf and on the Nile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> From <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot springs</a>, geothermal energy has been used for bathing since <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> times and for space heating since ancient Roman times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> Moving into the time of recorded history, the primary sources of traditional renewable energy were human <a href="/wiki/Manual_labour" title="Manual labour">labor</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_power" title="Animal power">animal power</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_power" title="Water power">water power</a>, wind, in grain crushing <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmills</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Firewood" title="Firewood">firewood</a>, a traditional biomass.
</p><p>In 1885, <a href="/wiki/Werner_von_Siemens" title="Werner von Siemens">Werner von Siemens</a>, commenting on the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_effect" title="Photovoltaic effect">photovoltaic effect</a> in the solid state, wrote:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In conclusion, I would say that however great the scientific importance of this discovery may be, its practical value will be no less obvious when we reflect that the supply of solar energy is both without limit and without cost, and that it will continue to pour down upon us for countless ages after all the coal deposits of the earth have been exhausted and forgotten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Max_Weber" title="Max Weber">Max Weber</a> mentioned the end of fossil fuel in the concluding paragraphs of his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Die_protestantische_Ethik_und_der_Geist_des_Kapitalismus" title="Die protestantische Ethik und der Geist des Kapitalismus">Die protestantische Ethik und der Geist des Kapitalismus</a> (The Protestant Ethic and the Spirit of Capitalism), published in 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> Development of solar engines continued until the outbreak of World War I. The importance of solar energy was recognized in a 1911 <i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a></i> article: "in the far distant future, <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">natural fuels</a> having been exhausted [solar power] will remain as the only means of existence of the human race".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup>
</p><p>The theory of <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">peak oil</a> was published in 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> In the 1970s environmentalists promoted the development of renewable energy both as a replacement for the eventual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depletion_of_oil" title="Depletion of oil">depletion of oil</a>, as well as for an escape from dependence on oil, and the first electricity-generating <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a> appeared. Solar had long been used for heating and cooling, but solar panels were too costly to build solar farms until 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renewable_energy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
